After the Collapse of the Xiang Embankment: Citizens of Eleven Counties Petition for Punishment of Negligent Officials; Failing to Enforce the Law Strictly is Insufficient to Appease Public Anger; Failing to Promptly Seek Remediation is Insufficient to Secure Order 74

Hankou Correspondence: Following the collapse of the Zhongxiang Xiang River embankment, the counties of Zhongxiang and others have once again suffered severe flooding. The authorities are diligently working on closing the breach and restoring the embankment in an attempt to salvage the situation. At the same time, they have requested punishment to clarify responsibility. Citizens from eleven counties to the north, believing the embankment collapse was due to the negligence of engineering personnel, have enumerated the points of dereliction and submitted separate appeals to the Executive Yuan (Jiang Yuan), Minister Jiang of the Ministry of Interior, the National Economic Council, the Director of the Pacification Headquarters, Chairman Yang of the Provincial Government, and High Commissioner Jiancha, lodging accusations and offering suggestions. The original petition, with representatives of the people, including Shen Bifang and others, listed as responsible, states approximately: The ten-plus counties downstream of the Xiang River in Hubei Province are the essence of the entire province, with a dense population and a large tax base, accounting for nearly one-half of the entire province. Last year, the Xiang embankment collapsed in Zhongxiang, and all eleven counties and cities, including Zhongxiang, Jingmen, Jingshan, Tianmen, Hanchuan, Anlu, Huangpi, Xiaogan, Yunmeng, Hanyang, and Hankou, suffered a devastating catastrophe. Receiving the government's concern for the people's suffering, substantial funds were allocated, instructing the Jianghan Engineering Bureau to construct a remote embankment, with Xi Dejiong as the director of the engineering office and Lin Youlong as the chief engineer, solely responsible for the project. Commissioner Shi Yuling served as the deputy director, and the county magistrates of Zhongxiang, Jingshan, Qianjiang, Tianmen, and Hanchuan served as coordinating members, supervising the laborers and working separately, which should have yielded satisfactory results. At the commencement of the remote embankment construction, Military Commission Chairman Jiang issued a major order stating that those who neglected the project would be dealt with by military law. The laborers, upon seeing this, were all terrified and cautious. Therefore, sections one, two, and three were supervised by the deputy director and the coordinating members, urging the laborers to work day and night, and were nearly completed. However, the fourth section was contracted out by the engineering office, colluding with the director of a certain private engineering firm, organizing the Jucheng Company, operating on a business basis, not using disaster laborers, but recruiting workers from afar in Anhui, Henan, and other places, only seeking profit. They did not use rammers, the loose soil was piled up carelessly, and the work was perfunctory. All measures were different from those in sections one, two, and three. Furthermore, a gap was left between sections fifty-six and fifty-seven of the fourth section, called a drainage ditch. Local officials and the people, upon seeing this, were all shocked and horrified. Although Your Honor, Provincial Chairman Yang, and Pacification Director He strictly ordered it to be filled, they secretly disobeyed. On May 26th, when the flood season arrived, the water-blocking dam first broke, followed by the water rushing out from the drainage ditch, and the water surged straight down, causing the downstream counties to suffer severe flooding again. This time, the embankment project mobilized several counties, lasted half a year, exhausted hundreds of thousands of laborers, and cost millions of dollars. The tangible and intangible losses to the people are even immeasurable. Now, we respectfully expose their crimes and thoroughly present them: The construction of the fourth section did not use civilian laborers, but adopted a contracting system, colluding with their private organizations to form companies, subcontracting layer upon layer, to make profits, which is their first crime. The civilian laborers had completed over 90% of the first, second, and third sections, but the contracted fourth section was only about 50% complete, as evidenced by Construction Director Liu's report after inspecting the remote embankment. Therefore, they delayed the project to wait for the flood season to come, which is their second crime. They only piled up loose soil and did not use rammers, the work was perfunctory, plotting to take advantage of the flood season to falsely report public funds during the emergency rescue, which is their third crime. They deliberately left a gap, which was not filled despite the instructions of various senior officials. They received the Yunxiang water level report and did not fill it for three days, waiting until the water-blocking dam collapsed and the water had reached the embankment before starting to rescue. Even important officials fled, making rescue impossible and construction unfeasible, which is their fourth crime. The original height of the cutoff dams for blocking the water flow was set at 45 meters. Construction Director Liu Shoupeng, Provincial Committee Member Fan Xiji, and Commissioner Shi Yuling of the Third District, fearing that the set height would not be able to withstand the summer flood in May, instructed the office to prepare sandbags and add a one-meter high sub-dam. The office ignored it, and the water level leaked through several holes at only 40.6 meters before reaching the Datantan, and then immediately collapsed, which is their fifth crime. The laborers recruited by the contractors were never sufficient, and there were also cases of deducting wages and unclear accounts of expenses, as evidenced by Committee Member Fan's report during the memorial week, which is their sixth crime. Summarizing the above six crimes, it is inexcusable. We should request Your Honor to strictly punish them in accordance with the Chairman's order to deal with them by military law. The fourth section has collapsed, the beans and wheat have been lost, the autumn harvest is hopeless, and the livelihood is cut off. The sounds of weeping shake the fields, and the sights are heartbreaking beyond description. Remediation should be promptly sought so that the remote embankment can be completed as soon as possible. If the water level rises during the summer and autumn rainy season, it will inevitably lead to a major disaster. The engineering personnel who have neglected their duties should be ordered to compensate for the construction costs and rescue the situation within a limited time, and success should be achieved by a deadline, without allowing any delays. We should promptly dispatch reliable personnel to be responsible for the rescue work to make up for the losses. Last year, the fellow-provincial associations of the disaster-stricken counties had planned to organize a Xiang Embankment Project Advancement Association to inspect the construction site, provide suggestions at any time, and ensure proper implementation, with the expenses borne by the local areas. At that time, Your Government had already appointed Director Xi as the director of the engineering office, Commissioner Shi as the deputy director, and the county magistrates as coordinating members, so it was not approved. Now, based on observations of the facts, such organizations are indeed necessary. We respectfully request that the disaster-stricken counties be allowed to organize an Advancement Association to facilitate progress and make the finances transparent to prevent corruption, in the hope of making up for the losses in the worst-case scenario. In short, the negligence of the office this time has turned the most essential area of the province into a swamp, causing millions of people to suffer the same disaster, and the loss of national revenue and the impact on finances are far from being comparable to ordinary dereliction of duty. Failing to enforce the law strictly is insufficient to appease public anger; failing to promptly seek remediation is insufficient to secure order. The urgent telegram is pressing, and there is no time to choose words. We humbly beg Your Excellency to consider it. (5th)

Educational Broadcasting Supplement

One of the Lectures on Biology: The Contribution of Biology to Mankind (Part 2) Xue Deyu, Director of the Natural Science Group of the Zhongzheng Bookstore Compilation and Translation Institute 76

Based on Pasteur's research, it was also known that the suppuration of all wounds was also caused by bacterial action, which opened a new era in surgery.

Pasteur's research on microorganisms directly affected our daily lives, because it was known that the spoilage of food and other organisms was mostly caused by microorganisms. At the same time, it was also known that microorganisms come from microorganisms. We can apply his principles, put food in tin cans, and use high temperature to kill the microorganisms hidden inside. Then, seal the tin cans and cut off air circulation so that bacteria have no way to enter, and the food in the cans can be stored for a long time without spoiling. This is the canned food sold on the market now. We can sit at home and taste fresh lychees and jackfruit at any time, or taste American milk and beef from across the ocean. This is thanks to the research of Leeuwenhoek and Pasteur. Therefore, the discovery of microorganisms and the establishment of cells are a great contribution to mankind.

The second contribution of biology to mankind is the expression of evolutionary thought, which makes mankind doubt how all living things evolved, and how they evolved from simple to complex. This is not only a great contribution to biology, but also its thought affects all sciences, and indicates the direction that mankind should take and solve all complex social problems.

In ancient times, all kinds of creatures were regarded as created by God. This kind of thought has long been deeply rooted in people's hearts. Until after the Middle Ages, people gradually knew that creatures come from creatures. Many people have doubted the theory of God's creation. Therefore, the French Cuvier came up with a theory of "catastrophism", believing that all kinds of creatures were originally created by God, but after thousands of years, the world changed, the hills and valleys changed, and a great change occurred. The creatures that lived on the ground died out, leaving only fossils buried in the ground. Then God created new creatures. Therefore, after each catastrophic change, the old creatures died and new creatures were born. The fossils found in the ground are of course very different from the existing creatures. This kind of thinking was later proven wrong as human intelligence gradually improved.

The first person to come up with evidence of opposition was the British geologist Lyell. He studied the structure of geology in detail and determined that the changes in geology were very slow, and there was no sign of a catastrophic change that would completely kill all living things. Therefore, Cuvier's theory, based on the facts reviewed by Mr. Mi, no longer has any basis for establishment.

The next person to publish the opposing theory was the French zoologist Lamarck, who believed that creatures could not be produced suddenly. Existing creatures have gradually changed and progressed from previous creatures, and the reason for their evolution lies in the "use and disuse" of organs. The more they are used, the more developed they are, and the less they are used, the more they degenerate. These more developed characteristics can be inherited by future generations. Lamarck's claim is like this, but after other scholars' experiments, the results are not all like this. For example, if you cut off a rat's tail, the tail of the rat born in the next generation will definitely not be shortened. Therefore, the German Weismann severely criticized Lamarck's theory, and strongly argued that the reason for the evolution of creatures does not lie in use or disuse. The theory that followed was Darwin's theory of evolution.

Darwin made long-term explorations and collections in the South Pacific and South America. Based on the collected materials, he published the theory of natural selection, saying in a nutshell: creatures reproduce in geometric progression, while food and other necessities only increase in arithmetic progression. There is an imbalance in supply and demand, so competition for survival arises. As a result, the fittest survive and the unfit perish. Originally, the characteristics that each creature receives from its parents are not fixed, and can gradually change. This is called variability. Because natural selection acts on variability, creatures can gradually evolve.

Darwin used the theory of natural selection to explain the cause of evolution. Recently, due to the progress of science, it is inevitable that it will be shaken. However, although the methods of explaining evolution often change, the fact of biological evolution never wavers. This is a point that I hope everyone will pay attention to.

Darwin's theory of evolution was published in the book "On the Origin of Species" seventy-seven years ago, and has at least two effects on biology.

The first effect is to prove the evolution of creatures by citing various facts. Before Darwin, scholars such as Cuvier and Lamarck all discussed the issue of biological evolution, but they were all empty ideas without factual proof, so they could not gain the belief of the world. Darwin was different. He presented various facts from morphology, anatomy, embryology, and paleontology (please refer to my book "The Facts of Biological Evolution" - published by Shanghai New Asia Bookstore), making the previous empty evolutionary theory into a factual proof. It also made the general public have the concept that creatures are indeed evolving, which cannot but be attributed to Darwin.

The first effect is to explain the cause of biological evolution. Past evolutionists only mentioned biological evolution, but did not think about the cause of evolution. Darwin further used "natural selection" to explain the theory of biological evolution. Although it has been gradually discovered that the fact that biological evolution cannot be completely proven by natural selection alone, Darwin's explanation of the cause of evolution caused many scholars to delve into this aspect, which cannot but be attributed to Darwin.

After the determination of biological evolution, it is known that humans were not created by God, but have gradually progressed upward from lower animals to reach today. Both now and in the future, they are advancing step by step along the path of evolution. Not only humans, but all living things and the natural world on which living things depend are gradually changing there. In other words, the idea of "daily renewal and daily renewal" is as surging as the theory of evolution, which is enough to inspire our spirit and move forward to a bright future.

The contribution of biology to life is of course not limited to the above two points, but "the establishment of cell theory" makes us know that all living things are born from living things. After the clarification of biological evolution, it makes us know that all living things gradually evolve from lower organisms to higher organisms, which is indeed the greatest contribution to our ideological world (End)

Page 8

Continuation of the Zhongxiang Xiang River Embankment Breach (Special Dispatch from Our Newspaper) The Engineering Office's Negligence in Key Projects is Undeniable; the Evils of the Contracting System Led to a Great Disaster 77

The Xiang River Embankment in Zhongxiang County, Hubei Province, unfortunately breached on the night of May 26th. The floodwaters turned fields and villages into ruins. Hundreds of thousands of families in Zhongxiang, Tianmen, and Hanchuan counties suffered another terrible calamity. The greatness and importance of this embankment were second to none in the country, except for the Yangtze and Yellow River embankments. The difficulty of its construction even surpassed the notoriously difficult Dongzhuang section of the Yellow River. Therefore, from the beginning of its repair, the National Economic Council, the Military Council Headquarters, and the Hubei Provincial Government all attached great importance to it. Chairman Chiang even issued a strict order that "military law will be applied to those who fail to repair the embankment." Now, the project is nearing completion, but it suddenly breached, and money and manpower were wasted. Although it was difficult to resist the great flood, it was also due to poor planning. The reporter stayed near the embankment for nearly a week. Amidst the vast expanse of water, I witnessed the tragedy of displacement and wandering, and felt grief upon hearing the news. Standing by the river, my sorrow increased. It is no wonder that when Fan Xiji and Shi Yuling and others surveyed the breach, they embraced and wept bitterly. Since the embankment protects the lives and property of eleven counties and cities, I have made a careful description of the planning and construction process, as well as the cause of this breach while on the embankment. This is something that those who care about the Xiang River embankment are eager to see first.

The Planning and Construction Process

The Han River enters Hubei Province from Shaanxi Province, passing through Xiangyang and flowing south to Zhongxiang. The water flow is rapid, bringing sediment. A slight overflow would turn ten counties, including Zhongxiang, Jingshan, Tianmen, Qianjiang, Hanchuan, Yunmeng, Yingcheng, Huanggang, Xiaogan, and Yangxin, into a watery country. Hankou would also be affected. In the past, a large embankment was built as a barrier. In early July of last year, there was torrential rain for five days and nights. The Xiang River suddenly rose by three zhang. Sections 18, 11, and 34 within Zhongxiang County successively collapsed. The breach in Section 34, which stretched for several miles, was the largest. The breached area was scoured into a river, connecting with the Yonglong River, forming a diversion of the Han River. The National Economic Council sent personnel to survey the area and proposed three designs: "opening a river," "restoring the old embankment," and "retreating and building a remote embankment." After repeated discussions by the Council, the Headquarters, and the Provincial Government, it was decided to retreat and build a remote embankment. In early November, the "Xiang River Embankment Engineering Office of the National Economic Council" was established in Hankou, with Lin Youlong as the chief engineer, to carry out surveying and construction. Later, due to the large scale of the project, it was feared that the chief engineer system would not be sufficient to cope with the situation. The organization was expanded with the approval of the National Economic Council, and Xi Dejiong, the director of the Jianghan Engineering Bureau, concurrently served as the director of the office, assisted by Shi Yuling, the administrative commissioner of the sixth district. Underneath, there were three sections: chief engineer, general affairs, and management. In December, the director and deputy director took office. On January 4th of this year, the Engineering Office moved to Shagang. As a result, banks, telegraph offices, hospitals, and shops were established one after another, and the wild banks and barren islands suddenly became bustling cities. The embankment repair plan was divided into two parts: one was the remote embankment project, and the other was the breach closure project. The remote embankment started from Jiukou and connected with the old embankment, passing through Shagang to Luohan Temple, with a length of 18 kilometers and 19 meters, divided into four sections and sixty subsections, each subsection being 300 meters long, about 13 meters high, and 7 meters wide at the top. The total earthwork required was 1.8 million cubic meters, and the original budget was more than 2.2 million yuan, which was increased to more than 2.7 million yuan due to the insufficiency. Sections 1, 2, and 3 were contracted by civilian laborers recruited from the five counties of Qianjiang, Tianmen, Zhongxiang, Jingshan, and Hanchuan. Each subsection accommodated at least 1,500 workers. The fourth section was contracted by self-recruited laborers. The breach closure project set up a breach closure section at Xiongjiaqiao, blocking the river in one place, with water-retaining dams at both ends. The right end was connected to Luohan Temple in the fourth section, called the A section water-retaining dam, and the left end was connected to Xinjishan, called the B section water-retaining dam. The total length was 5 kilometers, about 5 kilometers from Shagang. The dam top was 43.5 meters high, specifically to protect the remote embankment and prevent peach floods. Later, it was raised to 45 meters, and a sub-ridge was built on the dam to prevent wind and waves. Sections 1, 2, and 3 of the remote embankment started construction after the closure. By the time the embankment breached, 90% of it had been completed.

鍾祥遙堤潰冂　箭頭所示為潰堤之一端

Zhongxiang Remote Embankment Breach - The arrow indicates one end of the breached embankment

Past Project Deficiencies

From the beginning of the construction of the remote embankment, various obstacles arose due to the imperfections of the contracting system. The so-called contracting system was that the county governments were ordered to select contractors from each district, who were selected and employed by the Engineering Office, leading the laborers to work. The contractors had no management or command ability, and they were free to come and go as they pleased. In addition, the price was too low, and the laborers' food expenses were in deficit. The difference between the upper and lower parties accumulated day by day, and they could only borrow from the Engineering Office. At first, borrowing was difficult, but over time, cunning contractors took the opportunity to borrow excessively. Most of the laborers who came to the embankment were poor farmers who were forced to come by political forces. They could not cultivate their fields. When they first arrived at the embankment, it was during the severe winter season, and each person was only given two reed mats, which were not immediately available even after repeated requests. Moreover, the terrain was low and wet, and they slept on the grass. It was said that some people even froze to death before receiving the mats. As for the fixed price, regardless of the distance, it was initially four jiao per cubic meter. After deductions, the actual amount received was three jiao. Each person only earned a few fen or one jiao per day. Moreover, there was no rice to buy nearby, and temporary rice vendors hoarded the rice. Even this meager amount was not enough to satisfy one's hunger. And when there was wind, sand, rain, or snow, they could not work, and they gained nothing. They had no choice but to go hungry. Under the double pressure of hunger and cold, they disregarded everything and fled one after another. After escaping, they were chased and captured by local officials and brought back to the embankment. However, they could not endure hunger and cold, so they were forced to escape again, captured again, and so on more than ten times. The laborers suffered unspeakably, and the officials were exhausted. Those laborers who could barely support themselves mostly hired substitutes. It was estimated that the rural areas of the five counties of Zhongxiang and Jingshan lost no less than several million yuan. As a result, the people were restless, and the construction on the embankment was also slow. The Provincial Government, concerned that it would delay the key project, specially appointed Commissioner Fan Xiji to supervise the embankment. The National Economic Council also sent special commissioner Chen Ruzhen to supervise the embankment. Fan arrived at Shagang in early February and, after investigating the situation, ordered the engineering authorities to make vigorous improvements. He also changed to the Baojia system to manage the workers, using the layers of control of the district chief, the joint guarantee director, and the Baojia chief to supervise the laborers and work hard. The county magistrates of each county were stationed on the embankment to supervise the work. On the one hand, the price for taking soil from a longer distance was increased, rice was purchased, more reed mats were allocated, and relief was provided to the contractors who suffered losses. The laborers were then able to work with peace of mind, and the project progressed. However, much valuable time had already been wasted. After Fan changed the system on the embankment, Sections 1, 2, and 3 were completed first, while Section 4 was still contracted by the Engineering Office to recruit workers. The project was slower, and the soil taken was sandy, making the project less solid. The disaster of the breach was thus lurking here. Regarding the gains and losses of the project, the reporter also inquired in detail when he met Commissioner Shi on the embankment. Shi said that the Jianghan Engineering Bureau initially sent a document requesting that the contractors be moved and selected at Jiukou before December 5th of last year. They rushed to handle it day and night and arrived on schedule. Many laborers also went to work voluntarily. At that time, the Engineering Office stipulated that the price was too low and the distance for taking soil was too far, which could not maintain the lives of the laborers. Therefore, the contractors did not dare to contract, and the laborers who came to the embankment had no work to do, so they returned one after another. Later, the distance for taking soil and the price were slightly improved, and the laborers gathered again in late December. However, they still could not maintain their lives and fled again after a few days. For a month, it can be said that no construction was started at all. The Engineering Office never reported this situation. Later, after investigation, the Deputy Commander and the responsible section chief were sent to the embankment to investigate in the snow. This contracting system seemed to be recruiting workers but not recruiting workers, and seemed to be contracting but not contracting. There were too many shortcomings. In January, he personally led the county magistrates and district chiefs to be stationed on the embankment to supervise the work. However, due to the heavy snow and severe cold, too few reed sheds, and the laborers sleeping in the open air, the cries were extremely miserable, and the price of rice rose, making it difficult to have a full meal. They fled one after another, which also delayed the work a lot. He had no experience in embankment work. After being stationed on the embankment for several months, he felt that there were only two principles in making embankments: the embankment is made of soil, so it is necessary to pay attention to the soil source at all times; the soil is carried by the laborers, so it is necessary to pay attention to the food and housing of the laborers at all times, and try to maintain them. Unfortunately, the Engineering Office did not pay attention to this, etc.

Causes of the Embankment Breach

Sections 1, 2, and 3 of the remote embankment were able to proceed quickly under the supervision of the county magistrates, while Section 4 was slow to construct. This section passed through the Xincong River channel, making it difficult to take soil. It should have started construction in advance, but it was delayed until the end of January due to the blocking of the water-retaining dam. After the river was blocked on February 11th, the ground in Section 4 was completely drained, but it was still delayed for half a month before organizing work teams and soliciting contractors. The price was even lower than in Sections 1, 2, and 3. The closer ones were 5.6 jiao per cubic meter, which still had to be deducted for the expenses of the team leaders, etc., and divided among 46 people working, with 53 people sharing the cost. The exploitation of the contractors was even worse than in other sections, and the laborers all regarded it as a dangerous path. Among them, there were contractors who formed a company, contracting 1,200 meters, from subsection 55 to subsection 58, and planning to recruit 10,000 workers. Construction started on March 18th and was scheduled to be completed on May 8th. As a result, less than 3,000 workers were recruited, so the amount of earthwork in this subsection differed greatly. There was also a water channel of 5 or 6 feet wide left in subsection 96, which was not blocked for a long time. The breach occurred in this section. The failure to seize the opportunity led to a major disaster, which cannot but make people feel regret. After the water-retaining dam breached, the water rushed directly into Section 4 through the old river channel. At that time, there were only a few thousand workers there, and the materials were insufficient, so they could only wait for the breach. After the breach was surveyed, it was 530 meters long. According to the section chief of this section, Ye Yushin, he heard on the morning of the 26th that there was a flash flood in the upper reaches of the Han River, so he concentrated 10,000 workers from the entire section to rush to build the main drainage ditch and repair the low and thin embankment body of the entire section to resist it. At 6 pm, the height was built to 45 meters. After 9 pm, when the water reached the foot of the embankment, he ordered the workers to take soil from inside the embankment to increase the height. However, this place was an old water trough, and the water flow was turbulent. Although sacks were thrown repeatedly and work was done, it was ultimately ineffective. At 10:40 pm, when the water level reached 44 meters, the foot of the embankment leaked, resulting in the breach. The total losses, in addition to about 50,000 cubic meters of earthwork, included 450 work sheds, 3,625 carrying poles, 5,000 loads of baskets, and 500 hoes. The deaths of the workers are also unavoidable. I am responsible for my dereliction of duty, and I have asked the Engineering Office for punishment, he said. A total of eight breaches occurred in the water-retaining dam. The first one was 110 meters long, the second one was 179 meters long, the third one was 201 meters long, the fourth one was 133 meters long, the fifth one was 62 meters long, the sixth one was 94 meters long, the seventh one was 155 meters long, and the eighth one was 238 meters long, totaling 1,172 meters. The section chief, Huang Yongcheng, said that all the breaches were overflowing, but the water marks on the sections that did not breach were still more than one meter away from the top of the embankment.

Breach Closure and Embankment Restoration Plan

When the embankment breached, Fan Xiji and Xi Dejiong were attending a flood prevention meeting in Nanjing, and Shi Yuling and Chen Ruzhen were in the province negotiating with Chairman Yang to increase the number of workers to assist Section 4. The embankment was the responsibility of Chief Engineer Lin Youlong, which was not enough to cope with the emergency. After the breach, Fan and Xi rushed back to Hankou. On the 28th, they arrived at Shagang one after another with Shi, Chen, and Wang Huzhen, the technical director sent by the National Economic Council. They exchanged opinions that night. On the 29th, they went to inspect the breaches together. In the evening, they held another meeting to discuss in detail and decided to abandon the water-retaining dam and focus on blocking the breach in Section 4. Wang Huzhen drafted a plan, the steps being bundling boxes, advancing, and willow roller closure. The earthwork required was more than 87,000 cubic meters. The important materials were more than 73,000 bundles of reed grass, more than 45,000 loads of willow branches, 2,000 cubic meters of rubble, 30,000 sacks, 10,000 willow wood piles, 7,000 coils of rope, and 7,000 loads of wheat straw or rice straw. The budget was 600,000 yuan. It was scheduled that from the 1st to the 10th would be the material purchase period, and from the 11th to the 30th would be the breach closure period, with 20,000 laborers, regardless of sunny or rainy days, working hard day and night to complete the breach closure work in June. By July 15th, the entire embankment would be completed. Regarding the material problem, in addition to ordering the original five counties of Zhongxiang, Tianmen, Jingshan, Hanchuan, and Qianjiang to recruit laborers again, they also recruited from the seven counties of Yunmeng, Xiaogan, Yingcheng, Anlu, Mianyang, Dangyang, and Yicheng. The county magistrates or the secretaries of the sections supervised the arrival at the embankment. Fan Xiji and Shi Yuling convened a meeting of the county magistrates and district chiefs of each county and encouraged them to work hard to recruit workers. As for the presiding organization, the National Economic Council sent a telegram on the 2nd, proposing to reorganize the Engineering Office into the Xiang River Embankment Post-Disaster Relief and Flood Prevention Committee, with Fan Xiji presiding over the breach closure and Xi Dejiong and Shi Yuling assisting him, and to act expediently. Fan was ordered by the Provincial Government to supervise. After the motor failed, it seemed that direct supervision of the project had to be reconsidered. However, for the sake of the lives and property of the eleven counties and cities, Fan, who was courageous and responsible, might be ordered to take on the difficult task in times of crisis. It was found that the soil in this section was mostly loose sand, which would dissolve when it encountered water. The fact that the water did not reach the breach immediately was also due to the fact that the embankment soil contained too much sand. Now, the same mistake cannot be made again. If soil is taken from the mountains, at least seven people are required to make one cubic meter, which requires too much labor and is difficult to accommodate. The water level fluctuates constantly, and it is difficult to predict whether the project can be completed on schedule.

Songjiang: Traveler Commits Suicide in Hotel 78

A traveler wearing a silk short shirt and pants, claiming to be Feng Jinsheng from Jiaxing, 22 years old, stayed at the Datong Hotel on Songcao Road yesterday. He was sleeping soundly at night, and had not gotten up by 10 a.m. this morning. The waiter called him, but there was no response for a long time. He broke down the door and entered, and found that the traveler had committed suicide by hanging. His feet were kneeling on the toilet. Next to him was a suicide note, which stated that he was down on his luck, had no one to rely on, and was ashamed to return to his hometown. He asked for a simple burial and did not want anyone to be held responsible. There was a novel on the bed, which recorded the death of Emperor Chongzhen on Coal Hill. It was probably what the traveler was reading before he died. People said it was a coincidence. The hotel reported the incident to the police, who then requested the court to conduct an autopsy.

Suzhou: Zhouzhuang Robbed by Bandits 79

The Zhouzhuang Panlongxiang area in Suzhou is located on the edge of Cheng Lake and has always been a place where bandits emerge. At about 8 p.m. on the 6th, four bandit boats suddenly arrived in the township, carrying more than 50 bandits, each holding guns and other weapons. After landing, they set out in different directions to rob the farmers of the entire village. There were more than 20 farm families in the village, none of whom were spared. After about an hour of robbery, they were fully loaded and boarded the boat. Before leaving, they kidnapped Xu, the wife of farmer Zhou Fuqi, and her four-year-old child. They fired their guns as a show of force at the time. The loss was about 4,000 to 5,000 yuan. After the incident, the township's water patrol team immediately pursued them after hearing the report, but the bandits had gone far away and could not be caught. Therefore, they immediately reported to the Public Security Bureau. Director Zhang, after receiving the report, in addition to reporting to the county government for consultation with the water police team to assist in the arrest, also ordered the responsible sub-bureau and the detective team in July to strictly arrest the stolen goods and rescue the hostages. The 7th Brigade of the Provincial Security Forces stationed in Suzhou also sent a team to the township on the 7th to encircle and suppress the bandits.

Jiangyin: Shop Assistant Commits Suicide by Drowning 80

Geng Yusheng, a shop assistant at the Jixinchang general merchandise store in Jingjiang City (from Taixing), 20 years old, recently felt that the environment was bad. On the 31st, he took a river boat south. When the boat arrived in the middle of the river, he jumped into the river and committed suicide. Fortunately, the boat owner, Shi Xiaolai, rescued him and sent him to the Yidu Bureau, where his friend Zhang Linsheng accompanied him back to Jingjiang.

Wuxi: Yuanju Cocoon Firm Robbed 81

The Yuanju Cocoon Firm in Guyangfangqian Town, District 2 of the county, was originally established by Zi Cheng. Recently, it was rented to Zheng Cuichu and Ding Peiqing from Yangjian for business. It opened recently on the 6th. Everything was arranged in advance. The manager, Ding Peiqing, had 12,000 yuan in cash for cocoon purchases. On that day, 170 dan of fresh cocoons were received. At 9:45 p.m., some of the employees were already asleep when suddenly more than ten robbers arrived, wearing short clothes and armed with wooden shell guns and other weapons. The rest of the robbers were on guard outside. One robber went straight into the firm, first grabbed a young worker, fired a shot, and forced him into the accounting room, where he robbed all the 6,532 yuan of legal tender stored in the accounting cabinet (of which 300 yuan were one-jiao notes from the Xuzhou Official Mint Bureau). After the robbers obtained the silver dollars, they leisurely went in the direction of Meicun Dongting. Before leaving, they fired more than ten shots as a show of force. Because the firm had no police force to defend it, they dared not chase after them. They immediately telegraphed the Third Branch of the Public Security Bureau. After receiving the report, Zhang Songxun, the director of the Third Branch, immediately sent the police to pursue the robbers in three directions. They arrived at the Yuanju Cocoon Firm at 12 o'clock, but the robbers had already gone far away and nothing was gained. They immediately went inside to investigate and found four discarded shell gun bullets on the ground, which were immediately taken to the bureau for filing. Ding Peiqing, the manager of the firm, came to the city yesterday (the 7th) morning to report to the County Public Security Bureau and the Security Team and other agencies, requesting joint assistance in the arrest. It was heard that the firm had theft insurance with a certain insurance company in Shanghai, and they had already telegraphed the Shanghai firm to send someone to Wuxi to investigate. Also, Chen Xilian, a resident of Chenxiang Village in Zhaimenzhen, about five miles north of Zhangjingqiao in District 6, was a well-to-do family. On the evening of the 6th, three robbers arrived, holding a rifle, and broke down the door. The robbers went straight into the bedroom and arbitrarily searched for valuables. They were robbed of only eight yuan in legal tender. Before leaving, they fired four shots. Chen Xilian's wife, Xue Xueying (24 years old), jumped into the river through the back door to escape when the robbery occurred, resulting in her drowning. It was also tragic.

Jiashan: Ming Dynasty Tomb Discovered 82

North of the Yongning Nunnery in the county, a Ming Dynasty tomb was discovered the day before yesterday by the laborers building the Hangzhou-Hangzhou Highway there. It was of a grand scale, with a path overgrown with weeds leading to a passageway, with bricks and mortar peeling off on both sides. Inside the tomb were three coffins, all lacquered in blood-red. The middle coffin was covered with a half-rotten red banner, on which were written the words "Great Ming Shandong Investigating Censor, Canal Military Preparations Circuit". The handwriting was already blurred and difficult to recognize. The coffin on the left side was already rotten, and several pieces of stone meat and several copper coins were found in the coffin, as well as several other burial objects. The Security Team leader stationed at the Nunnery, Mou, led his team to protect the site, ordered that it be covered as before, and erected a sign to prevent others from looting it. According to nearby farmers, an old woman surnamed Luo from the Tingqiao Xiatang area in the city comes here every Qingming Festival to sweep the tomb.

Changzhou: Autopsy in Homicide Case 83

Gu Nangen, a farmer from Gujiacun, Longdexiang, District 4 of Wuyi, was called out by Gu Genda, a villager, on the 30th of last month. He did not return that night. The next morning, neighbors saw Nangen dead on the ground at his doorstep and hastily buried him. Later, his wife, Ding, suspected that her husband's death was suspicious and asked the township head to report it to the local court for an autopsy. Prosecutor Yang Kongyi arrived in the township on the 5th to open the coffin for an autopsy. The autopsy revealed that there was a blunt instrument wound on the left waist, overlapping blunt instrument wounds on the legs, and a ruptured kidney. He had died from the injuries he sustained before his death. After the autopsy, he summoned the neighbors for questioning and took Gu Gen, one person, to the city for interrogation and investigation.

Xiaoshan: Careless Silkworm Cocoon Drying Kills a Child 88

The family of a resident surnamed Gao near Dangshan in the eastern township of Xiaoshan suffered heavy losses because the price of silkworm cocoons raised in this year's session suddenly plummeted. Therefore, starting from the 5th, they decided to prepare to reel silk from the soil themselves and dried all the fresh cocoons themselves. Unexpectedly, at night, the fire from the stove spread to the mosquito net and instantly burned down three houses. Nine thatched houses were burned down in the two neighboring houses. A three-year-old girl from the neighboring Gao family, who was sleeping, could not escape and was buried in the fire. The total loss was worth four to five thousand gold, and more than 200 jin of fresh cocoons from the Gao family were all burned to ashes.

After returning to Xiangshan, he became even more rampant, strengthening his gang, shooting and killing Shanghai detectives, raping and looting, doing everything. He shot and killed the deputy township head in Cuijia'ao before. Recently, he joined forces with the notorious bandit Shen Heming, and his momentum has grown even greater. It is heard that Bandit Xie threatened to carry out large-scale kidnappings. Therefore, the wealthy households in Xiangdong are all on guard.

To the Editor,

I have recently read the news in your newspaper's Taicang Correspondence on June 1 regarding the strike in Yuewang City, which is not in line with the facts. Zhang Sentai has owed license tax for more than six seasons and has been contacted by the county government twice. He has been summoned many times but has not responded. Our director was inspecting and supervising the collection in Yue on that day and still sent the original police officer Ma Yongquan to summon him for questioning to persuade him. However, he deliberately resisted the tax and falsely claimed to have been beaten, inciting a strike. We have now submitted a request to the provincial department for investigation. We hereby request your newspaper to promptly correct this to set things right and clarify the truth.

Best regards,

Wu Gengyang, Director of the Jiatai Business Tax Bureau, June 5th.

Inauguration Ceremony of Huainan Railway; Sixth Anniversary of the Mining Bureau Celebrated Simultaneously; Over Two Hundred Chinese and Foreign Guests Attended 91

Bengbu Correspondence: The Huainan Coal Mining Bureau, directly under the Construction Committee, held its sixth-anniversary celebration and the inauguration ceremony of the Huainan Railway on the 5th of this month at Jiulonggang. Preparations had been underway for many days. Those invited to participate from Beijing, Shanghai, Bengbu, and Wuhu set off separately from the Bengbu and Wuhu routes on the 4th. Before 4 p.m., over two hundred Chinese and foreign individuals arrived at Jiulonggang, a bustling scene of great activity. At 4 p.m. that afternoon, the guests first visited various sections of the Dongjing (East Well) mining area, such as the overpass, derrick, coal washer, electric lighting room, air compressor room, and wellhead repair shop. They then visited the mechanical and electrical sections, such as the construction workshop, machine workshop, iron forging workshop, vehicle workshop, foundry workshop, material warehouse, and the new office building. Finally, they returned to the bureau to visit the exhibition room, which displayed souvenirs from various parties, coal samples from the East and West Wells, and products from along the Huainan Railway line. At 8 p.m., recreational activities were held to entertain the guests. All the guests stayed at the bureau that night, with the mining bureau dispatching police to guard the premises throughout the night for protection. At 8 a.m. on the 5th, the opening ceremony was held in the ceremonial hall in front of the bureau, with solemn formalities. The meeting was conducted as planned. The presidium of the assembly elected Qin Yu, director of the Construction Committee's Business Department, as the temporary chairman. He then reported the significance of holding the two ceremonies. Next, Pan Mingxin, director of the Construction Committee's Design Department, delivered a speech on behalf of Chairman Zhang Renjie of the committee. Following this, Cheng Shifan, director of the Huainan Coal Mining Bureau, reported on the development of the mine over the past six years and the construction of the railway over the past two years. Finally, Lu Chao, Chief Aide-de-Camp of the National Government; Guan Genglin, Director of the Ministry of Railways; Wu Zunming, representative of the Anhui Provincial Party Headquarters; Cao Shaoying, representative of the Anhui Provincial Government; Wu Qicheng, representative of the Bank of China in Nanjing; Gong Debai, president of the Jiuguo Ribao (National Salvation Daily); and Sun Yuanfu, representative of the Bengbu Chamber of Commerce, delivered speeches in succession. Around 11 a.m., Mrs. Wu Naili, wife of Qin Yu, performed the ribbon-cutting ceremony, and photographs were taken to commemorate the occasion. After the ceremony, the guests boarded special trains on the Bengbu and Wuhu routes and returned.

Local News

Various Industries Prevent Smuggling 92

Knitting Industry Association: The Shanghai Knitting Industry Association, in view of the rampant smuggling recently, has established a Joint Industry Anti-Smuggling Committee to prevent its intrusion. Yesterday, it issued the following announcement: "Since the rise of smuggling in North China, it has gradually spread to Central and South China. This not only affects our country's national tax revenue but also severely impacts our industrial and commercial sectors. It is a deeply distressing and malicious plan to undermine our country's economy. In order to assist the government in combating smuggling and to prevent the intrusion of smuggled goods, this association, after discussion, has established an Anti-Smuggling Committee. All colleagues in the industry must supervise each other and unanimously refuse to purchase smuggled goods. If there are those who are greedy for profit and forget their righteousness, secretly purchasing smuggled goods, anyone, or their associated partners, can report to the association and bear the responsibility of informing. Once conclusive evidence is found, we will request the government to impose severe sanctions. For informants, we will strictly maintain confidentiality and request the government to reward them. We hope that all our colleagues in the industry will work together to block smuggled goods and severely eliminate traitors in order to protect the strength of the country."

New Medicine and Pharmaceutical Manufacturing Associations: The New Medicine Industry Association and the Pharmaceutical Manufacturing Industry Association jointly proposed yesterday to establish a Research and Prevention of Smuggling Committee at the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce. This is to be approved at the Chamber of Commerce's membership representative conference on the 20th of this month and then submitted to the government for approval. The document stated: "National resources rely on tariff revenue for funding. Observing countries competing to build tariff barriers to support their own industries and commerce, it is evident that tariffs have the function of protecting domestic industry and commerce. Our country's industry and commerce have long suffered from the dumping of foreign goods and are already in a precarious state, relying heavily on the protection of tariffs. Moreover, foreign debt guarantees also rely heavily on tariff revenue, so the abundance or shortage of revenue greatly affects international credit. Recently, the rise of smuggling has become increasingly rampant, not only affecting tariff revenue and undermining the foundation of the national economy but also posing a major problem for our country's industry and commerce. Although the background is complex and suppression is not easy, the urgency of the crisis requires our industrial and commercial organizations to rise up and assist in researching methods to prevent smuggling, jointly removing internal obstacles so that foreign vagrants lose their reliance. We propose the establishment of a Research and Prevention of Smuggling Committee and request the government to issue an order to all chambers of commerce and industry associations across the country to mutually cooperate. Is this appropriate? We request a public decision."

National Goods Year Meeting for Citizens

The National Goods Year Committee for Citizens of this city, considering the increasingly serious smuggling in North China and the significant impact on domestic industries, has decided to convene a plenary meeting of the board of directors at 3 p.m. on the 10th to discuss implementation measures, in order to awaken citizens to use domestic goods. Yesterday, it notified all directors to attend, stating: "Regarding the increasingly serious smuggling in North China, domestic goods are being severely damaged and going bankrupt. In order to discuss expanding the publicity plan to awaken citizens to adopt domestic goods, we have scheduled a plenary meeting of the board of directors on the third floor of the Gongqiao Municipal Chamber of Commerce to discuss measures. We are specially notifying you to attend at that time to jointly discuss the implementation, which is important."

Minister of Foreign Affairs Zhang, who came to Shanghai to attend Mayor Wu's tea party and the annual meeting of the International Problems Research Association, took the night train to Beijing last night at 11 p.m. Accompanying him were Sun Ke, Peng Xuepei, Chen Jie, Zou Lin, Fu Bingchang, and others.

The Chinese Delegation to Siam Arrived in Bangkok Yesterday; The Foreign Ministry's Shanghai Office Received a Telegram Yesterday Stating That Inspections of Various Places Would Begin Today 94

The fifteen-member delegation of the Republic of China to Siam, led by head and deputy head Ling Bing and Lin Kanghou, departed from Shanghai on the French postal ship "Victoria" on the 26th of last month, arrived in Singapore on the 2nd of this month, and received a warm welcome from the local overseas Chinese. On the 4th, they transferred to Penang to go to Siam. It is now learned that the Foreign Ministry's Shanghai office received a telegram from the delegation in Bangkok yesterday, reporting that all members of the delegation arrived in Bangkok yesterday morning and will begin inspections on the 8th (today). After receiving the telegram, the office has forwarded letters to various agencies and organizations for their information.

Lawyers Association Held the Second Session of the Wrongful Imprisonment Compensation Movement Week Yesterday; Vigorously Advocating for Compensation System to Redress Wrongful Grievances; Hosting Various Sectors for Broadcasting and Speeches to Expand Publicity 95

The Shanghai Lawyers Association held the second anniversary conference of the Wrongful Imprisonment Compensation Movement Week at the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce in Tianhougongqiao yesterday (Sunday) at 3 p.m. It also hosted leaders from various agencies and organizations in the city. After the meeting, propaganda committee members were dispatched to various radio stations in the city to give speeches on the significance of wrongful imprisonment compensation. Lantern slides were also shown in various cinemas to promote the government's early formulation of wrongful imprisonment compensation regulations to protect the rights of those who have been wrongly accused. The details are recorded as follows:

Attendees

Guests included Guo Lanxin, representative of the Songhu Garrison Command; Zheng Yue from the Second Branch of the Jiangsu High Court; Huang Guorui from the Shanghai District Court; Deng Wu from the Shanghai First Special District District Court; Ding Yao from the Second Special District District Court; Mr. Wang, representative of Xu Fu, Director of the Municipal Finance Bureau; Yu Zhenxuan from the Shanghai Farmers Association; Xie Lin from the Accountants Association; Qu Shaoheng from the Shanghai Doctors Association; Mao Yun from the French Concession Taxpayers Association; Mao Xiaxuan from the Chinese Law Society; Sun Chucheng from the National Goods Factory Federation; Chen Jiufeng from the First Special District Citizens Association; and others. Members attending included Shen Junru, Chen Zhigao, Qu Yue, Wang Weizhen, Yang Zongliang, Mao Yun, Dong Chi, Ding Zhemeng, Zhang Juanxin, Zha Renwei, Yuan Yangan, Yu Chengxiu, Cai Zhaohuang, Yu Zufin, Yan Yinwu, Zhang Shijie, Wu Guochang, Xu Zuoliang, Zheng Wentong, Wang Manyun, and dozens of others.

Meeting Order

The meeting was opened with a bell. Shen Junru, Yu Chengxiu, Zhang Shijie, and others were elected to the presidium and took their seats. All guests and members stood up. A bow of respect was paid to the Party, the National Flag, and the portrait of the late Dr. Sun Yat-sen. Chairman Shen Junru respectfully read Dr. Sun Yat-sen's will. Three minutes of silence were observed. Chairman Shen Junru reported on the significance of today's Wrongful Imprisonment Compensation Movement and the progress of the movement over the past few years, actively uniting various sectors and unanimously advocating for the achievement of the government's early formulation of wrongful imprisonment compensation law. (Full text recorded later). Representatives from agencies and organizations, Zheng Yue (Second Branch of the High Court), Guo Lanxin (Garrison Command), Xie Lin (Accountants Association), Mao Xiaxuan (Chinese Law Society), and others spoke in succession. Yan Yinwu reported. Tea and refreshments were served, and the meeting adjourned.

Chairman's Report

Chairman Shen Junru reported, briefly stating that members were honored to have the participation of various officials and representatives of organizations. The motion was initiated at the 5th Representative Assembly of the Republic of China Lawyers Association in June of the 20th year of the Republic (1931), proposed by the association to request the Legislative Yuan to immediately promulgate the Wrongful Imprisonment Compensation Law. After passing, it was submitted to the government. By September of the following year, the 6th Representative Assembly was convened in Guangzhou, and the Guangzhou Lawyers Association continued to propose the organization of a Wrongful Imprisonment Compensation Movement Committee. After passing, 49 members of the Wrongful Imprisonment Compensation Movement Committee were appointed in the 23rd year of the Republic (1934), and a standing committee was established. Joint meetings with local lawyers associations were held repeatedly. On June 5th of the 24th year of the Republic (1935), the first National Wrongful Imprisonment Compensation Movement was held, requesting the government to promulgate this regulation as soon as possible. By September 20th of the 24th year of the Republic (1935), the entire judicial conference resolved to pass the Wrongful Imprisonment Compensation Law, which was sent to the Legislative Yuan for formulation. The Legislative Yuan has already handed it over to the Criminal Law Committee for reference. Last winter, a Wrongful Imprisonment Compensation Movement was convened in Hangzhou and passed, petitioning the Fifth National Congress. This year, the Third Wrongful Imprisonment Compensation Movement Committee requested the 7th Representative Assembly to continue to strive for it. Recently, the Fourth Wrongful Imprisonment Compensation Movement was convened in Jiangdu and passed, expanding publicity to promote the government's early implementation. Regarding the above process, the most important current matters are: Investigating whether there are wrongful imprisonments in various parts of the country, producing wrongful imprisonment statistics, and submitting them to the government for reference; the issue of recovering judicial rights is also important; regarding administrative and economic aspects, there are also many who are limited by the environment and lack the courage to make decisive decisions. However, we should unite with various sectors to urge the government to complete the Wrongful Imprisonment Compensation Regulations, so that they can be implemented on the same day as the Constitution, in order to improve the organization of the country. After the holding of this movement week, we should unanimously and firmly strive to achieve the goal of implementation.

Speeches Recorded Together

Next, Zheng Qian, Chief Prosecutor of the Second Branch of the High Court, spoke briefly, saying that the more civilized the society, the more crimes there are. The purpose of the court organization is to protect the interests of the people, etc. Next, Guo Lansheng of the Command spoke, saying that the Command is a military organization, and what it executes is mostly matters assigned by the judicial organs. However, it strongly agrees with the association's advocacy and is willing to follow up to promote its success, etc. Next, Qu Shaoheng of the Doctors Association spoke, saying that it is said that you all are committed to the Wrongful Imprisonment Compensation Movement, which is truly said to be something which touches the eye and moves the heart, and we sincerely hope that you will promote its success in order to reduce social injustice, etc. Finally, Mao Yun spoke, saying, We deeply wish that there would be no unjust matters in society, and if there are unjust matters, we should use the method of compensation to calm their hearts, etc. Then, Zha Dawei said that to seek a society without grievances, we should promote the rule of law and defeat imperialism. Yan Yinwu said that the Lawyers Association proposed the Wrongful Imprisonment Compensation draft, which was passed by last year's judicial conference and has been submitted to the Legislative Research Association by the Judicial Yuan for the Research Office to study, and then submitted to the Legislative Yuan for approval; expand the organization of the Legal Aid Association for the Poor, etc.

Broadcast Speeches

Last night at 8 p.m., the Wrongful Imprisonment Compensation Movement Seafarers Association dispatched broadcasting propagandists Zhang Shijie, Zhao Zhijiu, Yuan Yangan, Dai Jixian, Qian Jianqiu, Cui Shie, and others to send programs on the significance of the Wrongful Imprisonment Compensation Movement on various radio stations such as China West, Dongfang, Guohua, Donglu, Huaxing, Shanghai, and Lili. Excerpts from the speech are as follows: Today, the Shanghai Lawyers Association is sending representatives to broadcast on various radio stations. Listeners may think that what is being broadcast is legal common sense, but it is not. It is broadcasting the Wrongful Imprisonment Compensation Movement, which is closely related to the listeners. Why? Because Wrongful Imprisonment Compensation is to ask the state to formulate a law that allows people who have been wrongly accused to receive compensation for damages based on this law. A person, born into the world, is always inevitably wronged. Once wronged, after the grievances are redressed, all the losses suffered by those who have been imprisoned unjustly can be compensated by the state. Isn't it a great relationship with all the listeners? Asking the state to formulate this law is called the Wrongful Imprisonment Compensation Law. If a criminal defendant who is in custody is acquitted by a court judgment, or declared innocent, or exempted from prosecution for the crime he committed, then the state shall be liable for compensation for the damages he suffered during the period of detention. Even if he is convicted and executed, if he is declared innocent or acquitted or given a lighter sentence than the original judgment by the court in accordance with the retrial procedure or the extraordinary appeal procedure, the state shall also be liable for compensation for all damages during the period of detention or the execution of the sentence or the execution of the severe sentence. Although the main cause of wrongful imprisonment is the perjury of witnesses, or the false accusation of the accuser or the self-prosecutor, or the malfeasance of judicial officers, which leads to wrongful charges, the fault is not with the state, but the state should still be directly responsible for compensating the wronged person, and only the state can then recover the damages that should be compensated from the person who caused the wrongful imprisonment. This is called the corporate liability system. What we want to ask the state to formulate the Wrongful Imprisonment Compensation Law is based on this point, because judicial officers are officials appointed by the state, and judicial officers should be fair and honest in judging cases. If the cases judged by judicial officers are not fair and honest, so that the people are unjustly imprisoned, the scope of compensation is no more than two kinds of money and reputation. The damage to prisoners is also no more than these two kinds. As for those who have been executed and then redressed, there is no way to make the person who caused the wrongful imprisonment compensate with their lives, so we are assuming to require five compensation methods: A person who has been wrongly accused shall be given an amount of one yuan to five yuan per day according to the date on which he was accused; the money and goods wrongly fined shall be returned to him in full; If the goods are wrongly confiscated, they shall be compensated at the price; those who have been wrongly sentenced to death should be given living expenses to the dead's surviving family; if the dead's surviving family has the ability to live on their own and there is no need for education, they should be given consolation money; if the reputation is damaged due to the wrongful accusation, the compensation ruling should be published in the newspaper for apology.

Film Promotion

Last night, before the screening of the films, all the cinemas in the city showed the lantern slides made by the Wrongful Imprisonment Compensation Movement Committee of the Shanghai Lawyers Association, and the important significance of the Wrongful Imprisonment Compensation Movement was made into simple and clear words, which were first screened for a few minutes, so that the audience could clearly understand the importance of the early formulation and implementation of the Wrongful Imprisonment Compensation Law, etc.

The Authorities Pay Attention to the Recovery of Pilotage Rights; However, Almost All of the Pilots in Tongshan are Foreigners 96

The Central News Agency reported that, according to a reporter's inquiry to relevant parties on the issue of recovering pilotage rights, China did not pay much attention to pilotage rights in the past, so they have fallen into the hands of foreigners for decades. In recent years, China has gradually paid attention, and the Ministry of the Navy now has a pilot training institute to cultivate talents. There are already more than 200 graduates of the institute serving in various places. The four ministries of the Navy, Transportation, Finance, and Staff have established a Pilotage Management Committee in order to pay attention to all matters concerning pilots. All those engaged in pilotage must register and take examinations with the committee, so a part of the pilotage rights has been recovered. However, the recovery of pilotage rights in Tongshan outside Songkou is still under discussion. In the past, there were more than 40 pilots in Tongshan, almost all of whom were foreigners. Due to various reasons, recovery will still take time.

Huadong News Agency reports that this year's summer grain has successively entered the market, and the prices are very optimistic. All provinces, cities, and counties have reported bumper harvests. The details of the news are as follows:

Japanese Merchants Buy Rapeseed

Japanese merchants have always paid close attention to China's agricultural products, with the desire for "Industrial Japan and Agricultural China." Wheat samples have arrived in Shanghai, with prices ranging from 4.5 yuan to 4.7 yuan. This year's overall harvest is good. Financial Industry is Busy

The grain market is quite active, and the financial community also believes that loans for agricultural breeding have shorter terms and less risk. Their business with the grain community has suddenly become busy.

After Zhejiang Released 60% of the Cocoons Purchased, Shanghai Silk Mills Started Operating; Approximately Twenty Mills Including Hengcang 98

After the Zhejiang Provincial Silk Control Committee retained cocoons purchased below the standard price, the Shanghai Silk Mill Industry Association telegraphed requesting their release. Now, the Zhejiang Silk Control Committee has not only released 10%, but has also sampled and tested the cocoon yield in order to determine the penalty method. As for the 60% that was released earlier, it has been shipped to Shanghai one after another. Approximately twenty mills in Shanghai, such as Hengcang and Xinchang, have started reeling silk. Currently, the silk price in the European and American markets for B-grade standard Chinese silk is approximately 550 yuan per dan (a unit of weight) in national currency.

China's Silk Industry's Exports Decreased Sharply This Year 99

Shenshi News Agency reports that silk is a major export of China, world-renowned, and quite developed. However, since exports suddenly decreased sharply this year, the future is quite pessimistic. The main reasons are: 1. The increase in import tariffs by various countries; 2. The contraction of purchasing power abroad; 3. The lack of perfection in technology; 4. The dumping of Japanese silk. Therefore, in the European and American markets, etc., the number of exports this spring has decreased compared with last year. Last year's exports were 336,643 kilograms, worth 3,768,817 yuan in national currency. This year's exports during the same period were only 225,299 kilograms, worth 2,783,901 yuan in national currency. The decrease in quantity is 111,344 kilograms, and the decrease in value is 984,916 yuan. Moreover, because the US import tax on Chinese silk has been increased to more than 60%, and the lowest tax rate in other countries has also reached 30%, at the same time, since Central Europe such as Germany implemented controlled exchange, many obstacles have arisen for the collection of payment for goods. Moreover, the markets in Nanyang, India, and other places have also been seized by Japanese goods due to dumping. Therefore, China's silk industry should strive for innovation in production and sales, otherwise the future will be very bleak.
