"Shen Bao" Local Supplement

Talks

Rumors Caused by Increased Troop Deployments in North China 190

— Jing

Due to increased troop deployments by a certain party in the recent days in the Tianjin and Peiping areas, rumors have suddenly emerged, and the people are in a state of panic, as if they cannot live through the day. However, the content of the rumors is rarely reported in newspapers, making it impossible to know. Yesterday, the authorities in the North issued a statement, claiming that the current steps to deal with the situation are: internally, to strengthen spiritual unity and work hard on local construction; externally, to prioritize peace, and to conduct all matters based on the principles of equality, mutual benefit, and mutual respect for sovereignty. However, the extraordinary situation and the state of unrest in North China in recent days have all been caused single-handedly by a certain party. The responsibility for the rumors should be borne by that party. The authorities have compromised and explained their policies, originally out of good intentions, but truly out of desperation.

Loving peace is inherently a characteristic of the Chinese people, and "it is better to have one less thing than one more" has become a Chinese proverb. However, mutual benefit and mutual respect must be based on facts. Now, a certain party is increasing troop deployments every day, engaging in smuggling everywhere, and still using peace and friendship as a pretext, which is no different from playing with infants. I wonder, under what circumstances can it be said that there is no peace and no friendship? Is peace and friendship really like this? If a certain party deceives us in the name of peace and friendship, and we still deceive ourselves in the name of peace and friendship, it is perhaps understandable that others deceive us, but it is extremely unwise for us to deceive ourselves.

Compromising and seeking completeness originally stems from desperation, but compromising and seeking completeness must also have a considerable limit, and it is not simply about compromising and seeking completeness in everything. The current situation of compromising and seeking completeness is probably thousands of times beyond the appropriate limit. Moreover, compromising and seeking completeness means that compromising must seek completeness. If compromising cannot seek completeness, it is better not to compromise. The ancients had a saying, "Better to be a shattered jade than an intact tile." I would go one step further and say, it is understandable if the tile can remain intact, but if this continues, I fear that the tile will no longer be able to remain intact.

As the saying goes, "Even mosquitoes need to lay yellow eggs," meaning that the emergence of rumors must have a reason. Instead of repeatedly issuing statements to calm people's hearts, it is better to investigate the source of the rumors and make that party cease its unwarranted actions, so that the rumors will subside on their own. Otherwise, the more the rumors are suppressed, the more aggressive that party will become, and the more uneasy people will feel. Therefore, as the saying goes, "The one who tied the bell must untie it."

Not only that, but now there is also the so-called bombing case on the Beining Railway. It is still under investigation as to which party caused it and who carried it out, so it is impossible to know. However, according to a Havas report, the British Liberal Party's News Chronicle criticized the incident, saying that "the bombing case on the Beining Railway is exactly the same as the bombing of the railway tracks near Shenyang in 1931. The previous bombing resulted in the creation of a puppet state, and this bombing also happened to occur on the day when a certain party's plan to increase troop deployments in North China was completed." If this is the case, then that party is not only unwilling to eliminate rumors, but is also creating rumors every day. I ask, how can the rumors be quelled?

The Boss's Daughter (II) 191

— Ai Tu

When she was directing the workers with the air of a woman, she scolded them as if she were fierce:

"What! How many plates in total, how much money?"

That voice was simply a scream!

At first, we found her voice annoying, but as we observed her day by day, we felt a sadness that pierced our souls. Yes, that's right. Look at her all day, like a prisoner being watched by her parents, sitting in the accounting counter, staring at everything dull and devoid of childlike innocence. The cars on the road stirred up arrogant dust, ruthlessly assaulting that still-childlike face.

"Why don't you smile?" we teased her.

"Don't bother people! Who wants to smile like you?"

She pursed her small lips and screamed as if she were bursting out with angry flames. Her face was full of anger, and the breath of innocence had long been devoured by demons! Perhaps her lively heart was frustrated by this kind of life.

"However, shouldn't you be smiling? Your mother still smiles, and she's not as fierce as you!"

She was almost about to cry, and her eyes were red.

"Little girl, if you don't smile more in the spring, then you will be forever silenced, and you will demand a happy soul!"

This sentence stimulates the souls of all people in the universe who are without happiness.

She suddenly, as if in rebellion, slapped the table:

"Get out of here, you have to tease me! Drunkard!"

Like a heartbroken woman, tears flowed down, exhausted, with no more anger.

In this way, we were silent afterward, looking at her wounded face, sighing.

Early Summer 192

— Leng Yan

"Early summer is a season without sorrow."

I don't know which gentleman said that. Literary youths in Shanghai often enjoy writing about autumn and spring. I understand the reason for this: young people's emotions are rich, and spring and autumn are seasons that easily evoke sentiments. Isn't lamenting spring and grieving autumn a major part of Chinese literature?

As for me, I am most delighted by early summer. Spring is full of flowers and brocades, which are indeed very beautiful, but because there are flowers everywhere, in red and purple, I can't help but feel "tedious," and to put it bluntly, it is somewhat "vulgar." For example, a young girl, although very charming, ultimately cannot get rid of a petty air in her "demeanor."

Autumn has long been likened to a plain-dressed widow by the ancients. Clear, sparse, and distant, it is not without charm, but glancing around always makes one feel depressed and unhappy. Only in early summer, after the tea roses bloom and the flowers are gone, the green trees are shady and thick, which is very pleasant, like a young woman who has just removed her makeup, with her forehead hair all brushed up, bright and smooth, making people feel relaxed. However, this kind of goodness cannot be understood by young men and women. Even for myself, it has only been in the last year or two that I have truly understood the goodness of early summer.

It has been three or four years since I left the countryside. Recalling this time, green seedlings are everywhere, shady summer trees extend from nearby to the horizon. The rural area at noon is so quiet that there is no sound. If you bring a book alone and read it by the stream, letting the water and wind flow through your hair, you will definitely feel an indescribable joy. At this time, you don't have to immerse yourself in the sea of ​​fantasy. The current scenery is really too comfortable and satisfying for you.

Yes, early summer is indeed sleepy weather. If you really feel sleepy while reading a book, then you might as well lean against a tree and doze off. Anyway, there is a clear and loud cuckoo sound to wake you up. It not only wakes you up, but also uses its cry to refresh you. Because its cry is neither as trivial as the oriole's nor as melancholic as the cuckoo's, its cry is equally filled with the brightness of early summer.

It often flies from afar, its cry resounding from the horizon to the clouds. It slowly moves away, its cry resounding from the clouds back to the horizon. Gradually, it can't be heard anymore, and then the universe returns to the tranquility it had before.

In the evening, the countryside in early summer is even more peaceful. The smoke from cooking fires is so light that it is invisible, and waterwheels everywhere are singing happily, with water droplets splashing like flying jade. Then the strong young men sing, singing of the hardships of life, singing of the intensity of love, but when they are intoxicated by the current scenery, they also praise the rice seedlings and the cuckoos.

Beautiful scenery often makes people forget about work, but early summer does not make people indulge. It is only full of the pleasure of life. Just from this point of view, the praise of early summer is already certain.

Early summer is as described above in the countryside. In fact, early summer is even more wonderful in the courtyard. "Green banana trees divide the green onto the window gauze," heavy curtains hang down, tea and chess are leisurely, leaning wearily against the north window, the spirit meets with the ancients. "Paper screens don't pillow on bamboo square beds, tired of throwing books for a long midday nap." The ancients wrote many leisurely poems and prose at this time. As for "cities," the expression of the season is only on the clothing of women, because early summer is neither cold nor warm, or it may be a bit more active. I can't know for sure.

"Early summer is a season without sorrow."

Images of a Tea Room 193

—

Drizzle 194

— Er He

When Zhao Erbo looked up, the rain had become finer. He took his旱烟管 (hanyanguan, dry tobacco pipe) from the horizontal bar of the table. From a dark tobacco pouch, he pinched a wad of tobacco with his long fingers, then gathered it into a ball in his left palm and stuffed it into the pipe's head. He slowly lit it, and then two thick wisps of smoke billowed from his nostrils.

When he looked up again, the rain had become even finer. His tightly furrowed brow gradually relaxed like a banana leaf after the rain.

"Probably won't rain again, right?" he muttered to himself, smiling. A wave of yellow flashed before his eyes; he saw large ears of wheat.

Unconsciously, he increased the force with which he smoked, and the wisps of smoke that billowed from his nostrils were even thicker. "Hiss, hiss," there was a rhythmic, subtle sound on his pipe's head, which happened to be under the counter. Therefore, in the thin darkness, the firelight on the pipe's head rose and fell with the "hiss, hiss" sound. He was waiting, waiting for the rain to stop so he could go to the field ridge to have a look.

However, it seemed as if Heaven was deliberately mocking him: the rain gradually increased again. This made him anxious; the joy of earlier had been shattered by the sound of the rain. He hated the endless rain, which had been falling for so many days. Wouldn't it ever stop? He knew that these days were crucial for both the wheat harvest and the planting of rice. The wheat stalks had grown very well; it looked like there would definitely be a good harvest. However, the ears of wheat had only just emerged. Without adequate sunlight, constantly drenched in the rain, they would only grow stalks, and the ears would not be filled. If the ears of wheat were not filled, the harvest would of course be reduced. Furthermore, judging from the current situation, the reduction would be substantial. He scratched the top of his head with his right hand, sighing helplessly:

"Everything's turned upside down! This year is worse than the last!"

He packed another pipe with tobacco. He was usually somewhat stingy with tobacco, but his heart was truly too bitter. Without burning some tobacco, he simply couldn't settle himself down. At the same time, looking at the bright ashes he had just knocked out, he felt as if saving a match could compensate him for it. Without hesitation, he began to smoke his second pipe.

As he smoked, the rain still fell intermittently, sometimes heavy, sometimes light, sometimes stopping, sometimes continuing.

Last year, the wheat had all been destroyed by hail. This year, it was about to be harvested, but unexpectedly, there were seven or eight days of continuous rain. He thought of his family, who were finding it difficult to make a living, and his brow furrowed even more tightly. He had lived for over fifty years, and he had never seen harvests like these in recent years: either there was drought, or there was flooding; if there wasn't flooding, then there were insect plagues. A pile of terrifying darkness congealed before his eyes. He knocked out the ashes from his second pipe, stood up, and looked at the sky. The sky was dark and gloomy; the rain had only become a little lighter.

Braving the drizzle, he walked towards the field ridge. His feet were quite muddy, and there was a constant danger of falling down. His feet always couldn't stand firmly. He grieved for his aging, and he thought of his prime. He couldn't help but mutter to himself: "The sun is going to set anyway; the sun is going to set anyway!" (Note) However, the power of life encouraged him. No matter what, he had to continue living. He carefully and safely reached his own wheat field. He stroked the wheat stalks as if stroking a beloved but unfortunate child.

The wheat stalks had grown very tall. He knew that this wasn't a good sign; he knew that the ears of wheat this year would definitely not be filled, and there would definitely be a large discount. So his brow furrowed tightly.

Although it was a drizzle, it slowly soaked his torn coat. He looked at the western sky; his only hope was that it wouldn't rain again from this moment on. Lonely and desolate, he slipped and slid his way back home on the muddy road.

In the evening, he packed a pipe with tobacco, turned off the kerosene lamp, and was about to lie down in bed when he heard the sound of rain hitting the thatched roof very loudly. His brow furrowed tightly again, and another pile of terrifying darkness congealed before his eyes. "Hiss, hiss," he took a few forceful puffs and knocked out the ashes. Then, without sparing it, he smoked a second pipe. He knew that he definitely wouldn't be able to sleep tonight.

Note—"The sun is setting" alludes to the approach of death.

Song of the Earth 195

— Zhu Lu

The earth is vast

A gust of gray sand blew past, and the earth unfolded vaguely, the boundless earth developing in all directions.

The ground is full of deep yellow soil, as vast as the sea, the land stretching straight into the haze, as if connecting to the gray horizon.

Under the azure sky, the earth unfolded greatly and turbulently, the sun caressing the yellow mud tenderly. On the soil, in a winding snake-like path, traces of running feet have accumulated.

The earth recalls the past.

In the earth, the skulls of many ancestors have been buried and rotted, and in the soil, the blood and sweat of slaves for many years has seeped in. It contains the hardships of one year after another, costing the efforts of many serfs. Generations of people are buried in it, just like moths fluttering their wings, throwing themselves into the flames.

In the earth, the bitterness of generations of farmers has been buried. Farmers, laboring hard from childhood to old age, their blood and sweat flowed down day by day, like pearls, fertilizing the soil, cultivating the barren land into a hot one. The bodies of the farmers withered, but the earth gave birth to the fruits of cultivation. The farmers trembled and shoveled the mud, from dawn to night, from the bright spring to the cold and freezing sky. Their blood ran out, their energy was exhausted, until they collapsed painfully on the ground.

In the earth, ancient heroes also galloped on horseback, iron hooves trampled the mud and galloped past. Under the fluttering banner, strange soldiers on both sides went crazy and fought and killed each other. Purple-red blood flowed in the low-lying areas, accumulating into rivers, endless skulls exposed on the ground, the land was barren, until the serfs who were not killed and jumped out returned to cultivate the land, enduring generations of the same fate.

In the earth, the tears of sad mothers and women were also poured in, containing deep thoughts in their hot tears. They missed their children and husbands without any news. They lost their closest relatives, shivering in empty arms with heart-rending pain. Every day, hot tears dripped down, giving birth to wildflowers, and on every tomb, there were small wildflowers like specks of blood.

The earth is vast, as if there is no end.

The earth is like a vast, boundless cradle, where people grow up and die, and the earth is like an old grandmother, where children grow up in her arms, and then throw themselves into her wrist, burying their remains, everyone to the end--each one returns to the homeland!

The earth is silent, and when a gust of wind blows, the entire earth roars.

There was a time when the land was aging.

In the autumn season -

In the thin sunset, farmers girls, with blue floral headscarves, leapt vividly on the earth. Each one welcomed the wind, her arms constantly withdrawing, from her palms scattered grains of seeds. Their faces were full of the light of youth.

They spread seeds, their wide sleeves pregnant with wind, each one with sturdy chests, plunging into the gale, the headscarves fluttering, and each daughter of the earth was constantly stretching out her beautiful arms.

The barren land accepted and conceived.

The sky slowly dimmed.

A tramp immersed in darkness in the distance stared blankly at the farmers women active on the earth, and he was deeply moved. His lonely heart was filled with a surge of energy.

He stared with widened eyes.

He prostrated himself on the ground in excitement,

In the dark, his mouth covered down, tightly against the deep yellow soil...

Kisses the earth reverently.

Suzhou People (17) 197

— By Gu Wenzong

Liya: Enough, stop making fun of me, I'm already feeling bad enough!

Jinghong: Alright, my little princess, stop feeling bad. Losing money and being cheated is just a one-time thing. What good does feeling bad do? If you ruin your precious health, that's no laughing matter.

Liya: I really hate the deceptive tactics of these merchants. They spare no expense to create deceptive advertisements everywhere. Look, wherever the railway passes, it's all advertisements. The advertisements in public places are even more eye-catching than in secluded areas. Especially in Shanghai, there isn't a single street without advertisements. The rooftops of those tall buildings are also provided to merchants as advertising markets because of the potential for profit. It's simply an advertisement world!

Jinghong: The more advertisements there are, the more it shows that the market is not prosperous. To have a prosperous market, of course, you need to use the power of advertising to promote and expand outward. I just mentioned it a little earlier, advertisements are not necessarily deceptive. Some advertisements are indeed proof of cheap and beautiful goods. Moreover, these genuine advertisements are easily obscured by false advertisements because merchants who deceive customers with false advertisements must make their advertisements more eye-catching than genuine advertisements. The wording of the advertisements is also newer than others, and the number of advertisements is relatively increased in terms of length and position, even extending to various provinces and counties. Therefore, genuine merchants, standing in a position of commercial competition, can never watch their businesses fail. Of course, they must also expand and enlarge their advertising efforts to make their advertisements able to compete with the other party. In this way, the commercial field becomes a battlefield! Trade becomes a commercial war. But once you become a merchant, you have to follow the way of commerce. Once we understand this point, we should be lenient and just let it go. Why get upset over these insignificant things? This is all my fault, I brought you out and caused you to feel so upset. Now, you just need to believe that the big dishes are completely British style, and that's all, stop doubting it.

National Studies 198

Hu Zhangzhao, "Analects—Eight Rows"

Traffic (1300) 9:30 PM to 10:00 PM

Someone asked about the meaning of the Di sacrifice. Confucius said, "I do not know. He who knows its meaning would govern the world as easily as pointing to this," pointing to his palm. "Worship as if they were present; worship the spirits as if the spirits were present." Confucius said, "If I do not participate in the sacrifice, it is as if I did not sacrifice."

Wangsun Jia asked, "What does it mean to say, 'Rather pay court to the hearth than to the inner corner'?"

Confucius said, "It is not so. If you offend Heaven, there is nowhere to pray."

Confucius said, "Zhou observed the two dynasties. How rich and splendid its culture was! I follow Zhou."

Confucius entered the Grand Temple and asked about everything. Someone said, "Who says that the son of Zou knows ritual? He enters the Grand Temple and asks about everything." Confucius heard this and said, "This is ritual." Confucius said, "In archery, one does not pierce the hide; it is because the strength of the competitors is different. This is the ancient way." Zihua wanted to remove the sacrificial sheep from the announcement of the new moon. Confucius said, "Ci, you love the sheep, but I love the ritual."

Confucius said, "To serve the ruler with complete ritual is considered flattery."

Duke Ding asked how a ruler should employ his ministers and how ministers should serve their ruler. Confucius replied, "The ruler should employ his ministers with ritual, and the ministers should serve their ruler with loyalty."

Xu Wenbi Opening

Tongle (720) 1:00 PM to 1:45 PM

Opening "Climbing Mount Tai"

Mount Tai, the Eastern Peak of China, is famous. It has been praised for generations as a scenic spot. The mountain spirit nurtures the beautiful cliffs. Leisurely clouds and wild cranes form shade with the trees. The Tai'an Dai Temple is majestic. The Han cypress has stood for thousands of years. Climbing the mountain temple takes several miles. The Daizong Archway stands tall on the mountain screen. The White Crane Spring flows without a leak. The Jade Emperor Pavilion and the Cave of the True Man. The Wuxian Tower is surrounded by incense. Yellow tiles and red walls straddle the road. The Doumu Palace is praised as beautiful. The nuns are also charming. The Water Curtain Cave, a thousand veins compete to flow rapidly. The South Heaven Gate, a misty waterfall approaches. Listen closely. Turn east. The poor mountain people chatter incessantly. Tourists spend generously. The Two Tiger Temple. The Middle Heaven Gate. The climb to Dai has already gone halfway up. Food stalls sell food. The food is satisfying and without meat. Pass the happy three miles road. The winding path is like the road to Shu. Walking gracefully by the Cloud Step Bridge. The waves splash and ring like bells. The First Emperor Qin enjoyed the rain here in those years. The remains of the Five Great Men still exist in the Jianyi Pavilion. The pine mountains, pairs of Qin pines salute each other. The trees extend along the road, green and green. The Eighteen Bends, winding and difficult to step on. The stone steps on both sides are densely layered. The South Heaven Gate is built along the mountain. Shops line the Heavenly Street. The Bixia Palace of the Song Dynasty is large. Bronze tablets and stone tablets are lined up on both sides. The Jade Emperor Peak rises above the clouds. Ten thousand books come to court, only I am supreme. Climb to the top of Mount Tai. Look far from the Fengshan Terrace. The Qin Emperor was unkind and burned books, and the wordless monument stands at the top of the mountain for thousands of years. Look east at the sunrise from the Sunrise Peak. The Moon Peak, faces west and the moon is bright. The Cliffs of Sacrifice, the walls of the cliffs are dangerous as if walking on thin ice. The Old Man Peak, crouches and stands like a human. The scenery of Mount Tai is endless. The snow should remain in spring. Enjoy the journey and leave footprints.

Publishing Industry: The United Publishing House at 523 Xiafei Road will open on the 10th. It is currently distributing Oriental Literature, Overseas Literature, Dongliu, Monthly Literature, Poetry Monthly, Cultural Relics, Small Translation Series, International Education, International Trends, Oriental Public Opinion, Japanese Studies, Youth Culture, and various series of single books.

"Silver Song and Dance Music" will be published on the 10th of this month. The content includes famous songs from films such as "The Romantic Fleet," "Swallows Lean on New Makeup," and "Circular Song." Both simple and staff notations are listed, and all are printed with high-quality paper and a three-color copperplate cover. The price is only 20 cents per copy. Bookstores, music stores, or schools that want students to sell on commission can contact Lu's Publishing House at 11, Lane 50, Xiamen Road, Shanghai, or the Times Bookstore on Fuzhou Road.

Zhang Yuqing's "Bookworm" is a children's literature reading with brand new content, containing 19 "interesting" and "flavorful" fairy tales. The entire book has more than 100,000 words, with illustrations by Niubizi, making it very suitable for elementary and junior high school students to read. It is also a story reference book needed by parents and teachers. The actual selling price is 26 cents, distributed by Wenguang Bookstore in Yideli, Zilai Street. Major bookstores are acting as agents.

The long detective novel "Zhide Case" (written by Zheng Lejun), which was published in the Dasheng Daily yesterday, will be published by Zhengda Bookstore on Aiduo Ya Road on July 1st. The price is 40 cents, and the pre-order price is 20 cents. The pre-order period is from the 4th to the 15th of this month.

Lianhua Tidbits 202

Xu Jian has returned to Shanghai a few days ago to shoot "Go to Nature."

After Han Langen starred in the comedy short film "Sleepless Night," he has recently suffered from insomnia. Han has requested that Wu Yonggang, the film's director and screenwriter, be responsible for his medical expenses.

After Shang Guanwu's success in starring in "Tianlun," he is now working with Fei Mu again. In "Cold Moon Wolf Smoke Record," Shang plays the father of Li Lili.

Ren Guang and An E compose music for "Lost Lamb" and made many specially made scores.

Li Lili whistles a very beautiful song in "Go to Nature."

Shanghai Grand Theatre's Amazing Contribution 203

The Shanghai Grand Theatre has been showing the first round of special blockbusters composed of three united films since yesterday.

"The Origin of Man 1": This is a description of human evolution, based on Darwin's famous work depicting the beginning of the world and the beginning of mankind, a true and accurate performance. "The Beginning of Man" narrates the grand view of modern civilization and rare treasures.

"Photography News": It is a newsreel that has never been seen before. Everything that is terrifying, frightening, and startling is factual and heard. Everything that is considered an "impossible" film to shoot will clearly show all the amazing events in the world to the audience in a very short period of time. It can be boasted that "only Universal Pictures can shoot this" Photography News.

"Chinese Fitness Women": It is a completely domestic blockbuster. At this time of the expansion of women's rights, this film is very beneficial to Chinese women. The content includes various sports, healthy beauty, and nude sports, as well as a most valuable "production" that is regarded as taboo. In this film, it is shown to the audience very clearly with educational guidance.

Annie Taylor Louise and Alexander play a couple in "Young Couple" who are busy talking about love and forgetting to seek life.

Cathay Screening

Xu Qinfang Joins Yihua 204

Yihua's new work, "Little Sisters," directed by Xu Suling, is a tragedy set against a family background, depicting the love story of a pair of sisters, starring Little Bird Yuan Meiyun. Among them, there is a role playing Yuan Meiyun's stepmother. It was originally planned to hire Zhou Wenzhu to play the role, but the negotiations failed, so it has now been decided that Xu Qinfang will play the role. Xu Qinfang was a healthy and beautiful star with a large audience in the past. This return to the screen with a brand new image and creative style has attracted much attention from the audience.
